Task instruction sent to agent 
# Task: Extract Shared Foreach Optimizer Step

## Objective
Extract the repeated `_multi_tensor_*` foreach optimization patterns from individual
optimizer files (sgd.py, adam.py, adamw.py, etc.) into a shared
`torch/optim/_foreach.py` module.

## Requirements

1. **Create `torch/optim/_foreach.py`**:
   - `_foreach_optimizer_step(params, grads, step_fn, **kwargs)` function
   - Common foreach/fused parameter handling logic
   - Shared gradient scaling and clipping utilities

2. **Update optimizer files** to use the shared module:
   - `torch/optim/sgd.py`
   - `torch/optim/adam.py`
   - `torch/optim/adamw.py`
   - Others that have `_multi_tensor_` functions

3. **Keep backward compatibility**: existing public APIs unchanged

## Key Reference Files
- `torch/optim/sgd.py` — `_multi_tensor_sgd` function
- `torch/optim/adam.py` — `_multi_tensor_adam` function
- `torch/optim/adamw.py` — `_multi_tensor_adamw` function
- `torch/optim/_functional.py` — functional optimizer implementations

## Success Criteria
- `torch/optim/_foreach.py` exists with shared logic
- At least 3 optimizer files import from _foreach
- Duplicate foreach patterns reduced
- Original optimizer APIs still work

def _multi_tensor_rmsprop(
    params: list[Tensor],
    grads: list[Tensor],
    square_avgs: list[Tensor],
    grad_avgs: list[Tensor],
    momentum_buffer_list: list[Tensor],
    state_steps: list[Tensor],
    *,
    lr: float,
    alpha: float,
    eps: float,
    weight_decay: float,
    momentum: float,
    centered: bool,
    maximize: bool,
    differentiable: bool,
    capturable: bool,
    has_complex: bool,
):
    if len(params) == 0:
        return

    assert not differentiable, "_foreach ops don't support autograd"

    # If compiling, the compiler will handle cudagraph checks, see note [torch.compile x capturable]
    if not torch.compiler.is_compiling() and capturable:
        capturable_supported_devices = _get_capturable_supported_devices()
        assert all(
            p.device.type == step.device.type
            and p.device.type in capturable_supported_devices
            for p, step in zip(params, state_steps)
        ), (
            f"If capturable=True, params and state_steps must be on supported devices: {capturable_supported_devices}."
        )

    lr = _to_scalar(lr)

    grouped_tensors = Optimizer._group_tensors_by_device_and_dtype(
        [params, grads, square_avgs, grad_avgs, momentum_buffer_list, state_steps]  # type: ignore[list-item]
    )
    for (
        (
            grouped_params_,
            grouped_grads_,
            grouped_square_avgs_,
            grouped_grad_avgs_,
            grouped_momentum_buffer_list_,
            grouped_state_steps_,
        )
    ), _ in grouped_tensors.values():
        grouped_params = cast(list[Tensor], grouped_params_)
        grouped_grads = cast(list[Tensor], grouped_grads_)
        grouped_square_avgs = cast(list[Tensor], grouped_square_avgs_)
        grouped_state_steps = cast(list
... (truncated)

Analyze the common patterns and structures in the `_multi_tensor_*` foreach functions across PyTorch optimizers.

5. What utilities from the base Optimizer class they use
6. Common imports and type checking patterns

Provide a summary of:
- The most common operations and utility functions used across multiple _multi_tensor_ functions
- Code that is duplicated or very similar across files
- The main algorithm differences vs common infrastructure
- Opportunities for shared helper functions

## Summary of Analysis: Common Patterns and Structures in `_multi_tensor_*` Foreach Functions

Based on my analysis of the PyTorch optimizer implementations, here is a comprehensive summary of patterns found across all `_multi_tensor_*` functions:

### 1. **Files Containing `_multi_tensor_` Functions**
All 11 optimizer files contain multi-tensor implementations:
- `/workspace/torch/optim/sgd.py`
- `/workspace/torch/optim/adam.py`
- `/workspace/torch/optim/adamw.py` (reuses Adam)
- `/workspace/torch/optim/adagrad.py`
- `/workspace/torch/optim/adamax.py`
- `/workspace/torch/optim/adadelta.py`
- `/workspace/torch/optim/asgd.py`
- `/workspace/torch/optim/nadam.py`
- `/workspace/torch/optim/radam.py`
- `/workspace/torch/optim/rmsprop.py`
- `/workspace/torch/optim/rprop.py`
- `/workspace/torch/optim/_adafactor.py`

### 2. **Universal Function Signature Pattern**

All `_multi_tensor_*` functions follow this structure:
```python
def _multi_tensor_<optimizer>(
    params: list[Tensor],
    grads: list[Tensor],
    # various state tensors (momentum_buffer_list, exp_avgs, etc.)
    grad_scale: Optional[Tensor],
    found_inf: Optional[Tensor],
    *,  # keyword-only arguments follow
    # hyperparameters
):
```

**Common Parameters Across All:**
- `params`, `grads` (always present)
- `grad_scale`, `found_inf` (for AMP scaling support)
- Keyword-only hyperparameters

### 3. **Universal Opening Pattern**

Every `_multi_tensor_*` function starts with:

```python
if len(params) == 0:
    return

assert grad_scale is None and found_inf is None  # (except fused)

     1→# Plan: Extract Shared Foreach Optimizer Step Logic
     2→
     3→## Context
     4→PyTorch optimizers (SGD, Adam, Adagrad, etc.) all have `_multi_tensor_*` foreach implementations that handle batched parameter updates for performance. These 11+ optimizer files currently duplicate substantial amounts of common infrastructure code, making maintenance difficult and preventing consistent improvements.
     5→
     6→The goal is to extract repeated patterns into a shared `torch/optim/_foreach.py` module while maintaining 100% backward compatibility with public APIs.
     7→
     8→## Problem Statement
     9→**Current state:** 11 optimizer files each contain a `_multi_tensor_*` function with 200-400+ lines of code
    10→- Step counter updates (CPU optimization) - duplicated 8+ times
    11→- Weight decay + maximize pattern - duplicated 7+ times
    12→- Complex number conversion - duplicated 7+ times
    13→- Device/dtype grouping + casting - duplicated in every file
    14→- Sparse gradient checks - several files
    15→
    16→This duplication makes it difficult to:
    17→- Fix bugs consistently across all optimizers
    18→- Add features (e.g., AMP support) to all optimizers uniformly
    19→- Understand the core algorithm vs infrastructure code
    20→
    21→## Solution Overview
    22→Create a new `torch/optim/_foreach.py` module with reusable helper functions extracted from the common patterns identified across all `_multi_tensor_*` implementations.
    23→
    24→### Key Design Principles
    25→1. **Don't over-engineer**: Only extract code that is actually duplicated across 2+ optimizers
    26→2. **Keep algorithm-specific logic in optimizer files**: Each optimizer's core algorithm stays in its file
    27→3. **Focus on infrastructure**: Extract device/dt
... (truncated)

&\\rule{110mm}{0.4pt}                                                                 \\\\\n            &\\textbf{for} \\: t=1 \\: \\textbf{to} \\: \\ldots \\: \\textbf{do}                         \\\\\n            &\\hspace{5mm}\\textbf{if} \\: \\textit{maximize}:                                       \\\\\n            &\\hspace{10mm}g_t           \\leftarrow   -\\nabla_{\\theta} f_t \\nabla_{\\theta} f_t (\\theta_{t-1})          \\\\\n            &\\hspace{5mm}\\textbf{if} \\: \\lambda \\neq 0                                           \\\\\n            &\\hspace{10mm} g_t                                               \\\\[-1.ex]\n       \\end{aligned}\n\n    Nesterov momentum is based on the formula from\n    `On the importance of initialization and momentum in deep learning`__.\n    \"\"\"\n    + rf\"\"\"\n    Args:\n        {_params_doc}\n        lr (float, Tensor, optional): learning rate (default: 1e-3)\n        momentum (float, optional): momentum factor (default: 0)\n        dampening (float, optional): dampening for momentum (default: 0)\n        weight_decay (float, optional): weight decay (L2 penalty) (default: 0)\n        nesterov (bool, This is in contrast to some other\n        frameworks that initialize it to all zeros. One notable side effect\n        of this decision is that the first momentum value will not be scaled\n        by dampening. Dampening will be applied starting at the second step.\n\n    \"\"\"\n)\n\n\ndef sgd(\n    params: list[Tensor],\n    d_p_list: list[Tensor],\n    momentum_buffer_list: list[Optional[Tensor]],\n    # kwonly args with defaults are not supported by functions compiled with torchscript issue #70627\n    # setting this as kwarg for now as functional API is compiled by torch/distributed/optim\n    has_sparse_grad: bool = False,\n    foreach: Optional[bool] = None,\n    fused: Optional[bool] = None,\n    grad_scale: Optional[Tensor] = None,\n    found_inf: Optional[Tensor] = None,\n    *,\n    weight_decay: float,\n    momentum: float,\n    lr: float,\n    dampening: float,\n    nesterov: bool,\n    maximize: bool,\n):\n    r\"\"\"Functional API that performs SGD algorithm computation.\n\n    See :class:`~torch.optim.SGD` for details.\n    \"\"\"\n    # Respect when the user inputs False/True for foreach or fused. &\\hspace{5mm}m_t           \\leftarrow   \\beta_1 m_{t-1} + (1 - \\beta_1) g_t          \\\\\n            &\\hspace{5mm}v_t           \\leftarrow   \\beta_2 v_{t-1} + (1-\\beta_2) g^2_t          \\\\\n            &\\hspace{5mm}\\widehat{m_t} \\leftarrow   m_t/\\big(1-\\beta_1^t \\big)                   \\\\\n            &\\hspace{5mm}\\textbf{if} \\: amsgrad                                                  \\\\\n            &\\hspace{10mm} v_t^{max} \\leftarrow \\mathrm{max}(v_{t-1}^{max},v_t)                  \\\\\n            &\\hspace{10mm}\\widehat{v_t} \\leftarrow v_t^{max}/\\big(1-\\beta_2^t \\big)              \\\\\n            &\\hspace{5mm}\\textbf{else}                                                           \\\\\n            &\\hspace{10mm}\\widehat{v_t} \\leftarrow   v_t/\\big(1-\\beta_2^t \\big)                  \\\\\n            &\\hspace{5mm}\\theta_t \\leftarrow \\theta_{t-1} - \\gamma \\widehat{m_t}/\n                \\big(\\sqrt{\\widehat{v_t}} + \\epsilon \\big)                                       \\\\\n            &\\rule{110mm}{0.4pt}                                                          \\\\[-1.ex]\n            &\\bf{return} \\:  \\theta_t                                                     \\\\[-1.ex]\n            &\\rule{110mm}{0.4pt}                                                          \\\\[-1.ex]\n       \\end{aligned}\n\n    For further details regarding the algorithm we refer to `Adam: A Method for Stochastic Optimization`_.\n    \"\"\"\n    + rf\"\"\"\n    Args:\n        {_params_doc}\n        lr (float, Tensor, optional): learning rate (default: 1e-3). A tensor LR\n            is not yet supported for all our implementations. Please use a float\n            LR if you are not also specifying fused=True or capturable=True.\n        betas (Tuple[float, float], optional): coefficients used for computing\n            running averages of gradient and its square (default: (0.9, 0.999))\n        eps (float, optional): term added to the denominator to improve\n            numerical stability (default: 1e-8)\n        weight_decay (float, optional): weight decay (L2 penalty) (default: 0)\n        decoupled_weight_decay (bool, optional): if True, this optimizer is\n            equivalent to AdamW and the algorithm will not accumulate weight\n            decay in the momentum nor variance. (default: False)\n        amsgrad (bool, optional): whether to use the AMSGrad variant of this\n            algorithm from the paper `On the Convergence of Adam and Beyond`_\n            (default: False)\n        {_foreach_doc}\n        {_maximize_doc}\n        {_capturable_doc}\n        {_differentiable_doc}\n        {_fused_doc}\n    .. Note::\n        A prototype implementation of Adam and AdamW for MPS supports `torch.float32` and `torch.float16`.\n    .. _Adam\\: A Method for Stochastic Optimization:\n        https://arxiv.org/abs/1412.6980\n    .. _On the Convergence of Adam and Beyond:\n        https://openreview.net/forum?id=ryQu7f-RZ\n\n    \"\"\"\n)\n\n\ndef _single_tensor_adam(\n    params: list[Tensor],\n    grads: list[Tensor],\n    exp_avgs: list[Tensor],\n    exp_avg_sqs: list[Tensor],\n    max_exp_avg_sqs: list[Tensor],\n    state_steps: list[Tensor],\n    grad_scale: Optional[Tensor],\n    found_inf: Optional[Tensor],\n    *,\n    amsgrad: bool,\n    has_complex: bool,\n    beta1: Union[float, Tensor],\n    beta2: Union[float, Tensor],\n    lr: Union[float, Tensor],\n    weight_decay: float,\n    eps: float,\n    maximize: bool,\n    capturable: bool,\n    differentiable: bool,\n    decoupled_weight_decay: bool,\n):\n    assert grad_scale is None and found_inf is None\n\n    if torch.jit.is_scripting():\n        # this assert is due to JIT being dumb and not realizing that the ops below\n        # have overloads to handle both float and Tensor lrs, so we just assert it's\n        # a float since most people using JIT are using floats\n        assert isinstance(lr, float)\n        assert isinstance(beta1, float)\n        assert isinstance(beta2, float)\n    else:\n        lr = _to_scalar(lr)\n        # TODO: Support nonzero-dim Tensor betas, see #147921\n\n    # We only shuffle around the beta when it is a Tensor, otherwise, we prefer\n    # treating it as a scalar.\n    # Note: ensure type declaration is under conditional check for isinstance\n    # or else torchscript will get cranky about the DeviceDict type.\n    if isinstance(beta1, Tensor):\n        beta1_dict: Optional[DeviceDtypeDict] = {(beta1.device, beta1.dtype): beta1}\n    else:\n        beta1_dict = None\n\n    for i, param in enumerate(params):\n        grad = grads[i] if not maximize else -grads[i]\n        exp_avg = exp_avgs[i]\n        exp_avg_sq = exp_avg_sqs[i]\n        step_t = state_steps[i]\n\n        # If compiling, the compiler will handle cudagraph checks, see note [torch.compile x capturable]\n        if not torch.compiler.is_compiling() and capturable:\n            capturable_supported_devices = _get_capturable_supported_devices()\n            assert (\n                param.device.type == step_t.device.type\n                and param.device.type in capturable_supported_devices\n            ), (\n                f\"If capturable=True, params and state_steps must be on supported devices: {capturable_supported_devices}.\"\n            )\n\n        # update step\n        step_t += 1\n\n        if weight_decay != 0:\n            if decoupled_weight_decay:\n                # Perform stepweight decay\n                param.mul_(1 - lr * weight_decay)\n            else:\n                # Nested if is necessary to bypass jitscript rules\n                if differentiable and isinstance(weight_decay, Tensor):\n                    if weight_decay.requires_grad:\n                        grad = grad.addcmul_(param.clone(), weight_decay)\n                    else:\n                        grad = grad.add(param, alpha=weight_decay)\n                else:\n                    grad = grad.add(param, alpha=weight_decay)\n\n        if torch.is_complex(param):\n            grad = torch.view_as_real(grad)\n            exp_avg = torch.view_as_real(exp_avg)\n            exp_avg_sq = torch.view_as_real(exp_avg_sq)\n            if amsgrad:\n                max_exp_avg_sqs[i] = torch.view_as_real(max_exp_avg_sqs[i])\n            param = torch.view_as_real(param)\n\n        device = param.device\n\n        if beta1_dict is not None:\n            dtype = param.dtype  # type: ignore[union-attr]\n\n            # cast to workaround https://github.com/pytorch/pytorch/issues/140601\n            key = (device, dtype)\n            if key not in beta1_dict:\n                beta1_dict[key] = beta1.to(  # type: ignore[union-attr]\n                    device=device, dtype=dtype, non_blocking=True\n                )\n\n            device_beta1: Union[float, Tensor] = beta1_dict[key]\n        else:\n            device_beta1 = beta1\n\n        # Decay the first and second moment running average coefficient\n        exp_avg.lerp_(grad, 1 - device_beta1)\n\n        # Nested if is necessary to bypass jitscript rules\n        if differentiable and isinstance(beta2, Tensor):\n            if beta2.requires_grad:\n                # Using lerp to only use 2 operations bc addcmul's value cannot be a tensor\n                # Showing equivalence of differentiable path and nondifferentiable path\n                # expavg * b2 + grad^2 * (1-b2)\n                #           add expavg * (1-b2) - expavg * (1-b2) = 0\n                # expavg * b2 + expavg * (1-b2) - expavg * (1-b2) + grad^2 * (1-b2)\n                # expavg - expavg * (1-b2) + grad^2 * (1-b2)\n                # expavg + (grad^2 - expavg) * (1-b2)\n                # expavg.lerp(grad^2, 1-beta2)\n                exp_avg_sq.lerp_(torch.square(grad), weight=1 - beta2)\n            else:\n                exp_avg_sq.mul_(beta2).addcmul_(\n                    grad, grad, value=cast(float, 1 - beta2)\n                )\n        else:\n            exp_avg_sq.mul_(beta2).addcmul_(grad, grad, value=1 - beta2)  # type: ignore[arg-type]\n\n        if capturable or differentiable:\n            step = step_t\n\n            # Nested if is necessary to bypass jitscript rules\n            if differentiable and isinstance(beta1, Tensor):\n                if beta1.requires_grad:\n                    bias_correction1 = 1 - beta1 ** step.clone()\n                else:\n                    bias_correction1 = 1 - beta1**step\n            else:\n                bias_correction1 = 1 - beta1**step\n\n            # Nested if is necessary to bypass jitscript rules\n            if differentiable and isinstance(beta2, Tensor):\n                if beta2.requires_grad:\n                    bias_correction2 = 1 - beta2 ** step.clone()\n                else:\n                    bias_correction2 = 1 - beta2**step\n            else:\n                bias_correction2 = 1 - beta2**step\n\n            step_size = lr / bias_correction1\n            step_size_neg = step_size.neg()\n\n            bias_correction2_sqrt = bias_correction2.sqrt()\n\n            if amsgrad:\n                # Maintains the maximum of all 2nd moment running avg. till now\n                if differentiable:\n                    max_exp_avg_sq = max_exp_avg_sqs[i].clone()\n                else:\n                    max_exp_avg_sq = max_exp_avg_sqs[i]\n\n                max_exp_avg_sqs[i].copy_(torch.maximum(max_exp_avg_sq, exp_avg_sq))\n\n                # Uses the max. for normalizing running avg. of gradient\n                # Folds in (admittedly ugly) 1-elem step_size math here to avoid extra param-set-sized read+write\n                # (can't fold it into addcdiv_ below because addcdiv_ requires value is a Number, not a Tensor)\n                denom = (\n                    max_exp_avg_sqs[i].sqrt() / (bias_correction2_sqrt * step_size_neg)\n                ).add_(eps / step_size_neg)\n            else:\n                denom = (\n                    exp_avg_sq.sqrt() / (bias_correction2_sqrt * step_size_neg)\n                ).add_(eps / step_size_neg)\n\n            if differentiable:\n                param.addcdiv_(exp_avg.clone(), denom)\n            else:\n                param.addcdiv_(exp_avg, denom)\n        else:\n            step = _get_value(step_t)\n\n            bias_correction1 = 1 - beta1**step\n            bias_correction2 = 1 - beta2**step\n\n            step_size = lr / bias_correction1\n\n            bias_correction2_sqrt = bias_correction2**0.5\n\n            if amsgrad:\n                # Maintains the maximum of all 2nd moment running avg. till now\n                torch.maximum(max_exp_avg_sqs[i], exp_avg_sq, out=max_exp_avg_sqs[i])\n\n                # Use the max. for normalizing running avg. of gradient\n                denom = (max_exp_avg_sqs[i].sqrt() / bias_correction2_sqrt).add_(eps)\n            else:\n                denom = (exp_avg_sq.sqrt() / bias_correction2_sqrt).add_(eps)\n\n            param.addcdiv_(exp_avg, denom, value=-step_size)  # type: ignore[arg-type]\n\n        # Lastly, switch back to complex view\n        if amsgrad and torch.is_complex(params[i]):\n            max_exp_avg_sqs[i] = torch.view_as_complex(max_exp_avg_sqs[i])\n\n\ndef _multi_tensor_adam(\n    params: list[Tensor],\n    grads: list[Tensor],\n    exp_avgs: list[Tensor],\n    exp_avg_sqs: list[Tensor],\n    max_exp_avg_sqs: list[Tensor],\n    state_steps: list[Tensor],\n    grad_scale: Optional[Tensor],\n    found_inf: Optional[Tensor],\n    *,\n    amsgrad: bool,\n    has_complex: bool,\n    beta1: Union[float, Tensor],\n    beta2: Union[float, Tensor],\n    lr: Union[float, Tensor],\n    weight_decay: float,\n    eps: float,\n    maximize: bool,\n    capturable: bool,\n    differentiable: bool,\n    decoupled_weight_decay: bool,\n):\n    if len(params) == 0:\n        return\n\n    if isinstance(lr, Tensor):\n        if not capturable:\n            raise RuntimeError(\n                \"lr as a Tensor is not supported for capturable=False and foreach=True\"\n            )\n        if lr.numel() != 1:\n            raise ValueError(\"Tensor lr must be 1-element\")\n\n    if isinstance(beta1, Tensor):\n        if not capturable:\n            raise ValueError(\n                \"beta1 as a Tensor is not supported for capturable=False and foreach=True\"\n            )\n        if beta1.numel() != 1:\n            raise ValueError(\"Tensor beta1 must be 1-element\")\n\n    if isinstance(beta2, Tensor):\n        if not capturable:\n            raise ValueError(\n                \"beta2 as a Tensor is not supported for capturable=False and foreach=True\"\n            )\n        if beta2.numel() != 1:\n            raise ValueError(\"Tensor beta2 must be 1-element\")\n\n    # If compiling, the compiler will handle cudagraph checks, see note [torch.compile x capturable]\n    if not torch.compiler.is_compiling() and capturable:\n        capturable_supported_devices = _get_capturable_supported_devices(\n            supports_xla=False\n        )\n        assert all(\n            p.device.type == step.device.type\n            and p.device.type in capturable_supported_devices\n            for p, step in zip(params, state_steps)\n        ), (\n            f\"If capturable=True, params and state_steps must be on supported devices: {capturable_supported_devices}.\"\n        )\n\n    assert grad_scale is None and found_inf is None\n\n    assert not differentiable, \"_foreach ops don't support autograd\"\n\n    lr = _to_scalar(lr)\n    # TODO: Support nonzero-dim Tensor betas, see #147921\n\n    grouped_tensors = Optimizer._group_tensors_by_device_and_dtype(\n        [params, grads, exp_avgs, exp_avg_sqs, max_exp_avg_sqs, state_steps]  # type: ignore[list-item]\n    )\n\n    # We only shuffle around the beta when it is a Tensor and on CUDA, otherwise, we prefer\n    # treating it as a scalar.\n    beta1_dict: Optional[DeviceDict] = (  # type: ignore[attr-defined]\n        {beta1.device: beta1}\n        if isinstance(beta1, Tensor) and str(beta1.device) != \"cpu\"\n        else None\n    )\n\n    for (\n        device_params_,\n        device_grads_,\n        device_exp_avgs_,\n        device_exp_avg_sqs_,\n        device_max_exp_avg_sqs_,\n        device_state_steps_,\n    ), _ in grouped_tensors.values():\n        device_params = cast(list[Tensor], device_params_)\n        device_grads = cast(list[Tensor], device_grads_)\n        device_exp_avgs = cast(list[Tensor], device_exp_avgs_)\n        device_exp_avg_sqs = cast(list[Tensor], device_exp_avg_sqs_)\n        device_state_steps = cast(list[Tensor], device_state_steps_)\n\n        device = device_params[0].device\n        if beta1_dict is not None and device not in beta1_dict:\n            beta1_dict[device] = beta1.to(device=device, non_blocking=True)  # type: ignore[union-attr, attr-defined]\n\n        device_beta1 = beta1_dict[device] if beta1_dict else beta1\n\n        # Handle complex parameters\n        if has_complex:\n            if amsgrad:\n                device_max_exp_avg_sqs = cast(list[Tensor], device_max_exp_avg_sqs_)\n                _view_as_real(\n                    device_params,\n                    device_grads,\n                    device_exp_avgs,\n                    device_exp_avg_sqs,\n                    device_max_exp_avg_sqs,\n                )\n            else:\n                _view_as_real(\n                    device_params, device_grads, device_exp_avgs, device_exp_avg_sqs\n                )\n\n        if maximize:\n            device_grads = torch._foreach_neg(device_grads)  # type: ignore[assignment]\n\n        # Update steps\n        # If steps are on CPU, foreach will fall back to the slow path, which is a for-loop calling t.add(1) over\n        # and over. 1 will then be wrapped into a Tensor over and over again, which is slower than if we just\n        # wrapped it once now. The alpha is required to assure we go to the right overload.\n        if not torch.compiler.is_compiling() and device_state_steps[0].is_cpu:\n            torch._foreach_add_(\n                device_state_steps, torch.tensor(1.0, device=\"cpu\"), alpha=1.0\n            )\n        else:\n            torch._foreach_add_(device_state_steps, 1)\n\n        if weight_decay != 0:\n            if decoupled_weight_decay:\n                # Perform stepweight decay\n                torch._foreach_mul_(device_params, 1 - lr * weight_decay)\n            else:\n                # Reuse the intermediate memory (device_grads) already allocated for maximize\n                if maximize:\n                    torch._foreach_add_(device_grads, device_params, alpha=weight_decay)\n                else:\n                    device_grads = torch._foreach_add(  # type: ignore[assignment]\n                        device_grads, device_params, alpha=weight_decay\n                    )\n\n        # Decay the first and second moment running average coefficient\n        # Use device beta1 if beta1 is a tensor to ensure all\n        # tensors are on the same device\n        torch._foreach_lerp_(\n            device_exp_avgs, device_grads, cast(float, 1 - device_beta1)\n        )\n\n        torch._foreach_mul_(device_exp_avg_sqs, beta2)\n\n        # Due to the strictness of the _foreach_addcmul API, we can't have a single\n        # tensor scalar as the scalar arg (only python number is supported there)\n        # as a result, separate out the value mul\n        # Filed https://github.com/pytorch/pytorch/issues/139795\n        if isinstance(beta2, torch.Tensor):\n            scaled_device_grads = torch._foreach_mul(device_grads, 1 - beta2)  # type: ignore[assignment]\n            value = 1.0\n        else:\n            scaled_device_grads = device_grads  # type: ignore[assignment]\n            value = 1 - beta2\n\n        torch._foreach_addcmul_(\n            device_exp_avg_sqs, scaled_device_grads, device_grads, value\n        )\n\n        # Delete the local intermediate(s) since they won't be used anymore to save on peak memory\n        del device_grads\n        del scaled_device_grads\n\n        bias_correction1: Union[tuple[Tensor, ...], list[Tensor]]\n        bias_correction2: Union[tuple[Tensor, ...], list[Tensor]]\n        bias_correction2_sqrt: Union[tuple[Tensor, ...], list[Tensor]]\n\n        if capturable:\n            bias_correction1 = torch._foreach_pow(beta1, device_state_steps)  # type: ignore[arg-type]\n            bias_correction2 = torch._foreach_pow(beta2, device_state_steps)  # type: ignore[arg-type]\n            # foreach_sub doesn't allow a scalar as the first arg\n            torch._foreach_sub_(bias_correction1, 1)\n            torch._foreach_sub_(bias_correction2, 1)\n            # we do not negate bias_correction1 as it'll need to be negated later anyway\n            torch._foreach_neg_(bias_correction2)\n\n            # foreach_div doesn't allow a scalar as the first arg\n            torch._foreach_div_(bias_correction1, lr)\n            torch._foreach_reciprocal_(bias_correction1)\n\n            torch._foreach_sqrt_(bias_correction2)\n\n            # Re-assign for clarity as we maintain minimal intermediates: we'll have\n            # step_size = - lr / (1 - beta1 ^ t) where t = num_steps\n            # bias_correction2_sqrt = sqrt(1 - beta2 ^ t)\n            step_size = bias_correction1\n            bias_correction2_sqrt = bias_correction2\n\n            if amsgrad:\n                device_max_exp_avg_sqs = cast(list[Tensor], device_max_exp_avg_sqs_)\n                # Maintains the maximum of all 2nd moment running avg. till now\n                torch._foreach_maximum_(device_max_exp_avg_sqs, device_exp_avg_sqs)  # type: ignore[assignment]\n\n                # Set intermediate to the max. for normalizing running avg. of gradient when amsgrad\n                exp_avg_sq_sqrt = torch._foreach_sqrt(device_max_exp_avg_sqs)\n            else:\n                exp_avg_sq_sqrt = torch._foreach_sqrt(device_exp_avg_sqs)\n\n            torch._foreach_div_(exp_avg_sq_sqrt, bias_correction2_sqrt)\n            torch._foreach_add_(exp_avg_sq_sqrt, eps)\n            torch._foreach_div_(exp_avg_sq_sqrt, step_size)\n\n            # at this point, exp_avg_sq_sqrt = - (1 - beta^t) * [sqrt(exp_avg_sq / (1 - beta2^t)) + eps] / lr\n            torch._foreach_addcdiv_(device_params, device_exp_avgs, exp_avg_sq_sqrt)\n        else:\n            bias_correction1 = [\n                1 - beta1 ** _get_value(step) for step in device_state_steps\n            ]\n            bias_correction2 = [\n                1 - beta2 ** _get_value(step) for step in device_state_steps\n            ]\n\n            step_size = _stack_if_compiling([(lr / bc) * -1 for bc in bias_correction1])\n\n            bias_correction2_sqrt = [bc**0.5 for bc in bias_correction2]  # type: ignore[arg-type]\n\n            if amsgrad:\n                device_max_exp_avg_sqs = cast(list[Tensor], device_max_exp_avg_sqs_)\n                # Maintains the maximum of all 2nd moment running avg. till now\n                torch._foreach_maximum_(device_max_exp_avg_sqs, device_exp_avg_sqs)\n\n                # Use the max. for normalizing running avg. of gradient\n                exp_avg_sq_sqrt = torch._foreach_sqrt(device_max_exp_avg_sqs)\n            else:\n                exp_avg_sq_sqrt = torch._foreach_sqrt(device_exp_avg_sqs)\n\n            torch._foreach_div_(exp_avg_sq_sqrt, bias_correction2_sqrt)\n            torch._foreach_add_(exp_avg_sq_sqrt, eps)\n            torch._foreach_addcdiv_(\n                device_params,\n                device_exp_avgs,\n                exp_avg_sq_sqrt,\n                step_size,  # type: ignore[arg-type]\n            )\n\n\ndef _fused_adam(\n    params: list[Tensor],\n    grads: list[Tensor],\n    exp_avgs: list[Tensor],\n    exp_avg_sqs: list[Tensor],\n    max_exp_avg_sqs: list[Tensor],\n    state_steps: list[Tensor],\n    grad_scale: Optional[Tensor],\n    found_inf: Optional[Tensor],\n    *,\n    amsgrad: bool,\n    has_complex: bool,  # Needed for consistency.\n    beta1: float,\n    beta2: float,\n    lr: Union[float, Tensor],\n    weight_decay: float,\n    eps: float,\n    maximize: bool,\n    capturable: bool,  # Needed for consistency.\n    differentiable: bool,\n    decoupled_weight_decay: bool,\n) -> None:\n    if not params:\n        return\n    if differentiable:\n        raise RuntimeError(\"Adam with fused=True does not support differentiable=True\")\n\n    grad_scale_dict: DeviceDict = (\n        {grad_scale.device: grad_scale} if grad_scale is not None else {}\n    )\n    found_inf_dict: DeviceDict = (\n        {found_inf.device: found_inf} if found_inf is not None else {}\n    )\n\n    # We only shuffle around the lr when it is a Tensor and on CUDA, otherwise, we prefer\n    # treating it as a scalar.\n    lr_dict: Optional[DeviceDict] = (\n        {lr.device: lr} if isinstance(lr, Tensor) and str(lr.device) != \"cpu\" else None\n    )\n    grouped_tensors = Optimizer._group_tensors_by_device_and_dtype(\n        [params, grads, exp_avgs, exp_avg_sqs, max_exp_avg_sqs, state_steps]  # type: ignore[list-item]\n    )\n    for (device, _), (\n        (\n            device_params_,\n            device_grads_,\n            device_exp_avgs_,\n            device_exp_avg_sqs_,\n            device_max_exp_avg_sqs,\n            device_state_steps_,\n        ),\n        _,\n    ) in grouped_tensors.items():\n        device_params = cast(list[Tensor], device_params_)\n        device_grads = cast(list[Tensor], device_grads_)\n        device_exp_avgs = cast(list[Tensor], device_exp_avgs_)\n        device_exp_avg_sqs = cast(list[Tensor], device_exp_avg_sqs_)\n        device_state_steps = cast(list[Tensor], device_state_steps_)\n\n        device_grad_scale, device_found_inf = None, None\n        if grad_scale is not None:\n            device_grad_scale = grad_scale_dict.setdefault(\n                device, grad_scale.to(device, non_blocking=True)\n            )\n        if found_inf is not None:\n            device_found_inf = found_inf_dict.setdefault(\n                device, found_inf.to(device, non_blocking=True)\n            )\n        if lr_dict is not None and device not in lr_dict:\n            lr_dict[device] = lr.to(device=device, non_blocking=True)  # type: ignore[union-attr]\n            lr = lr_dict[device]\n        torch._foreach_add_(device_state_steps, 1)\n        func = torch._fused_adam_ if not decoupled_weight_decay else torch._fused_adamw_\n        func(\n            device_params,\n            device_grads,\n            device_exp_avgs,\n            device_exp_avg_sqs,\n            device_max_exp_avg_sqs,  # specific optimizers\n4. **LR conversion** - `_to_scalar()` normalizes tensor learning rates\n5. **Device/dtype grouping** - `Optimizer._group_tensors_by_device_and_dtype()` - critical for multi-GPU/multi-dtype support\n\n### 4. **Main Loop Structure**\n\nAll use this pattern:\n```python\nfor (device_params, device_grads, ...), _ in grouped_tensors.values():\n    device_params = cast(list[Tensor], device_params_)\n    device_grads = cast(list[Tensor], device_grads_)\n    # ... cast other states\n    \n    # Handle complex numbers if needed\n    if has_complex:\n        _view_as_real(device_params, device_grads, ...)\n    \n    # Core algorithm operations\n```\n\n**Casting Pattern:** All use `cast(list[Tensor], ...)` from typing module for type safety.\n\n### 5. **Common Algorithm Infrastructure**\n\n#### A. **Maximize Handling** (Very Common Pattern)\n```python\nif maximize:\n    device_grads = torch._foreach_neg(device_grads)\n```\n- Applied early in processing\n- Reuses intermediate memory when possible\n- Appears in: SGD, Adam, Adagrad, Adamax, Adadelta, ASGD, RMSprop\n\n#### B. **Step Counter Update** (Very Common Pattern)\n```python\n# If steps are on CPU, foreach will fall back to the slow path\nif not torch.compiler.is_compiling() and device_state_steps[0].is_cpu:\n    torch._foreach_add_(\n        device_state_steps, torch.tensor(1.0, device=\"cpu\"), alpha=1.0\n    )\nelse:\n    torch._foreach_add_(device_state_steps, 1)\n```\n- Optimization for CPU-based steps\n- Appears in: Adam, Adagrad, Adamax, Adadelta, ASGD, RMSprop, Rprop, NAdam\n\n#### C. **Weight Decay** (Universal Pattern)\n```python\nif weight_decay != 0:\n    if maximize:\n        # Reuse intermediate memory (device_grads) already allocated for maximize\n        torch._foreach_add_(device_grads, device_params, alpha=weight_decay)\n    else:\n        device_grads = torch._foreach_add(\n            device_grads, device_params, alpha=weight_decay\n        )\n```\n- Memory efficiency: Reuse grads buffer when maximize is already used\n- Creates new intermediate when maximize is False\n- Appears in: SGD, Adam, Adagrad, Adamax, Adadelta, ASGD, RMSprop\n\n#### D. **Sparse Gradient Handling**\n- SGD checks for sparse gradients and falls back to for-loop:\n  ```python\n  device_has_sparse_grad = has_sparse_grad and any(\n      grad.is_sparse for grad in device_grads\n  )\n  if device_has_sparse_grad:\n      # foreach doesn't support sparse\n      for i in range(len(device_params)):\n          device_params[i].add_(device_grads[i], alpha=-lr)\n  ```\n\n- Adagrad completely delegates to single-tensor version for sparse:\n  ```python\n  if device_has_sparse_grad:\n      _single_tensor_adagrad(...)\n      continue\n  ```\n\n#### E. **Complex Number Handling** (Very Common)\n```python\nif has_complex:\n    _view_as_real(device_params, device_grads, device_exp_avgs, ...)\n```\n- Converts complex tensors to real view\n- Applied at beginning of device loop\n- Uses utility function `_view_as_real()` from optimizer.py\n- Appears in: Adam, Adagrad, Adamax, Adadelta, ASGD, RMSprop, Rprop, NAdam\n\n#### F. **Capturable Mode Handling** (Complex Pattern)\nTwo different code paths:\n```python\nif capturable:\n    # Tensor-based operations, all on device\n    torch._foreach_pow(beta1, device_state_steps)\n    torch._foreach_sub_(bias_correction1, 1)\n    # ...\nelse:\n    # Extract values and use Python lists\n    bias_correction1 = [1 - beta1 ** _get_value(step) for step in device_state_steps]\n    step_size = [(lr / bc) * -1 for bc in bias_correction1]\n```\n- Capturable path: Uses tensor operations, no .item() calls\n- Non-capturable path: Extracts Python scalars via `_get_value()`\n- Appears in: Adam, Adamax, Adadelta, ASGD, RMSprop, Rprop, NAdam\n\n### 6. **Key Helper Functions from optimizer.py**\n\n```python\ndef _get_value(x):\n    \"\"\"Extract Python value from tensor, optimized for compilation\"\"\"\n    if torch.compiler.is_compiling():\n        return x\n    else:\n        return x.item() if isinstance(x, torch.Tensor) else x\n\ndef _to_scalar(x):\n    \"\"\"Convert multi-element tensor to 0-d scalar tensor\"\"\"\n    if isinstance(x, torch.Tensor) and x.dim() != 0:\n        return x.squeeze()\n    return x\n\ndef _stack_if_compiling(x):\n    \"\"\"Stack list into tensor only when compiling\"\"\"\n    if torch.compiler.is_compiling():\n        return torch.stack(x)\n    return x\n\ndef _view_as_real(params, *state_and_grads):\n    \"\"\"Convert complex tensors to real view for computation\"\"\"\n    for i, p in enumerate(params):\n        if torch.is_complex(p):\n            params[i] = torch.view_as_real(params[i])\n            for s in state_and_grads:\n                s[i] = torch.view_as_real(s[i])\n\n@staticmethod\ndef _group_tensors_by_device_and_dtype(tensorlistlist, with_indices=False):\n    \"\"\"Group tensor lists by (device, dtype) for efficient batch operations\"\"\"\n```\n\n### 7. **torch._foreach_* Operations Used Across Functions**\n\nMost common operations (appearing in multiple optimizers):\n\n**Unary operations (in-place):**\n- `torch._foreach_add_()` - scalar or tensor addition\n- `torch._foreach_mul_()` - scalar multiplication\n- `torch._foreach_sub_()` - subtraction\n- `torch._foreach_div_()` - division\n- `torch._foreach_sqrt_()` - square root\n- `torch._foreach_neg_()` - negation\n- `torch._foreach_reciprocal_()` - 1/x\n- `torch._foreach_abs_()` - absolute value\n- `torch._foreach_pow()` - exponentiation\n- `torch._foreach_maximum_()` - element-wise max\n\n**Binary operations (in-place):**\n- `torch._foreach_addcmul_()` - fused multiply-add: y += x1 * x2 * value\n- `torch._foreach_addcdiv_()` - fused divide-add: y += x1 / x2 * value\n- `torch._foreach_lerp_()` - linear interpolation\n\n**Copy/allocation:**\n- `torch._foreach_add()` - returns new tensor (not in-place)\n- `torch._foreach_mul()` - returns new tensor\n- `torch._foreach_sub()` - returns new tensor\n- `torch._foreach_sqrt()` - returns new tensor\n- `torch._foreach_abs()` - returns new tensor\n- `torch._foreach_maximum()` - returns new tensor\n\n### 8. **Memory Efficiency Patterns**\n\n#### A. **Reusing Intermediate Buffers**\n```python\n# Strategy: Reuse grads buffer for multiple operations\nif maximize:\n    torch._foreach_add_(device_grads, device_params, alpha=weight_decay)  # in-place\n    # grads now contains: -grad + weight_decay * param\n    # This buffer is reused for next operations\nelse:\n    device_grads = torch._foreach_add(device_grads, device_params, alpha=weight_decay)\n    # Creates new tensor, original grads not modified\n```\n\n#### B. **Temporary Buffer Deletion**\n```python\n# Explicitly delete large intermediates to free memory\ndel device_grads\ndel scaled_device_grads\n```\n- Appears in: Adam\n\n### 9. **Type Checking and Conversion Patterns**\n\n**Type casting:**\n```python\nfrom typing import cast, Optional, Union\n\ndevice_params = cast(list[Tensor], device_params_)\nstep_size: Union[tuple[Tensor, ...], list[Tensor]]\n```\n\n**Isinstance checks:**\n```python\nif isinstance(lr, torch.Tensor):\n    # Special handling for tensor learning rates\nif isinstance(beta2, torch.Tensor):\n    # Special handling for tensor betas\n```\n\n### 10. **Specific Algorithm Patterns**\n\n#### Adam Family (Adam, Adamax, NAdam, RAdam)\n```python\n# 1. Negate grads if maximize\n# 2. Add weight decay (optional)\n# 3. Update step counter\n# 4. Update exponential moving averages\n# 5. Compute bias corrections (capturable vs non-capturable paths)\n# 6. Update parameters\n```\n\n#### SGD with Momentum\n```python\n# 1. Negate grads if maximize\n# 2. Add weight decay (optional)\n# 3. Update momentum buffer (handle first step)\n# 4. Apply nesterov if needed\n# 5. Update parameters\n```\n\n#### Adaptive Methods (Adagrad, Adadelta, RMSprop)\n```python\n# 1. Negate grads if maximize\n# 2. Update step counter\n# 3. Add weight decay\n# 4. Update accumulator/second moment\n# 5. Compute adaptive learning rates\n# 6. Update parameters\n```\n\n### 11. **Compiler and JIT Support Patterns**\n\n```python\n# Check if compiling to Inductor\nif torch.compiler.is_compiling():\n    # Special handling for compiled code\n    torch._foreach_add_(device_state_steps, torch.tensor(1.0, device=\"cpu\"), alpha=1.0)\n    \nif not torch.compiler.is_compiling():\n    # Optimization for eager mode\n    if device_state_steps[0].is_cpu:\n        # Use explicit tensor wrapping for CPU\n\n# Torch.jit.script checks are mainly in dispatcher functions, not _multi_tensor_\n```\n\n### 12. **Opportunities for Shared Infrastructure**\n\nBased on the analysis, these operations could be factored into helpers:\n\n1. **Gradient preprocessing:**\n   ```python\n   def _preprocess_grads(grads, maximize, params, weight_decay):\n       \"\"\"Apply maximize negation and weight decay\"\"\"\n   ```\n\n2. **Step update:**\n   ```python\n   def _update_step_counters(state_steps, is_compiling):\n       \"\"\"Update step counters with CPU optimization\"\"\"\n   ```\n\n3. **Complex number handling:**\n   ```python\n   def _apply_complex_view(has_complex, *tensors):\n       \"\"\"View complex tensors as real if needed\"\"\"\n   ```\n\n4. **Capturable bias correction:**\n   ```python\n   def _compute_bias_corrections(betas, steps, capturable):\n       \"\"\"Compute bias corrections for both capturable/non-capturable paths\"\"\"\n   ```\n\n5. **Tensor grouping with cleanup:**\n   ```python\n   def _group_and_process(tensor_lists, processor_fn):\n       \"\"\"Group tensors and apply processing function\"\"\"\n   ```\n\n### 13. **Code Duplication Examples**\n\n**Most duplicated:** Step counter update pattern (8+ occurrences)\n**Second most:** Weight decay + maximize pattern (7+ occurrences)  \n**Third:** Complex number conversion pattern (7+ occurrences)\n\nThe most critical duplicated code is the CPU step counter optimization, which appears in nearly every adaptive optimizer to avoid repeated tensor allocations.",

185\u2192\n   186\u2192    Nesterov momentum is based on the formula from\n   187\u2192    `On the importance of initialization and momentum in deep learning`__.\n   188\u2192    \"\"\"\n   189\u2192    + rf\"\"\"\n   190\u2192    Args:\n   191\u2192        {_params_doc}\n   192\u2192        lr (float, Tensor, optional): learning rate (default: 1e-3)\n   193\u2192        momentum (float, optional): \\text{lr} * v_{t+1},\n   224\u2192            \\end{aligned}\n   225\u2192\n   226\u2192        where :math:`p`, :math:`g`, :math:`v` and :math:`\\mu` denote the\n   227\u2192        parameters, gradient, velocity, and momentum respectively.\n   228\u2192\n   229\u2192        This is in contrast to Sutskever et al. and\n   230\u2192        other frameworks which employ an update of the form\n   231\u2192\n   232\u2192        .. math::\n   233\u2192            \\begin{aligned}\n   234\u2192                v_{t+1} & = \\mu * v_{t} + \\text{lr} * g_{t+1}, \\\\\n   235\u2192                p_{t+1} & = p_{t} - This is in contrast to some other\n   242\u2192        frameworks that initialize it to all zeros. One notable side effect\n   243\u2192        of this decision is that the first momentum value will not be scaled\n   244\u2192        by dampening. Dampening will be applied starting at the second step.\n   245\u2192\n   246\u2192    \"\"\"\n   247\u2192)\n   248\u2192\n   249\u2192\n   250\u2192def sgd(\n   251\u2192    params: list[Tensor],\n   252\u2192    d_p_list: list[Tensor],\n   253\u2192    momentum_buffer_list: list[Optional[Tensor]],\n   254\u2192    # kwonly args with defaults are not supported by functions compiled with torchscript issue #70627\n   255\u2192    # setting this as kwarg for now as functional API is compiled by torch/distributed/optim\n   256\u2192    has_sparse_grad: bool = False,\n   257\u2192    foreach: Optional[bool] = None,\n   258\u2192    fused: Optional[bool] = None,\n   259\u2192    grad_scale: Optional[Tensor] = None,\n   260\u2192    found_inf: Optional[Tensor] = None,\n   261\u2192    *,\n   262\u2192    weight_decay: float,\n   263\u2192    momentum: float,\n   264\u2192    lr: float,\n   265\u2192    dampening: float,\n   266\u2192    nesterov: bool,\n   267\u2192    maximize: bool,\n   268\u2192):\n   269\u2192    r\"\"\"Functional API that performs SGD algorithm computation.\n   270\u2192\n   271\u2192    See :class:`~torch.optim.SGD` for details.\n   272\u2192    \"\"\"\n   273\u2192    # Respect when the user inputs False/True for foreach or fused.   204\u2192       \\begin{aligned}\n   205\u2192            &\\rule{110mm}{0.4pt}                                                                 \\\\\n   206\u2192            &\\textbf{input}      : \\alpha \\text{ (alpha)}, \\: \\gamma \\text{ (lr)},\n   207\u2192                \\: \\theta_0 \\text{ (params)}, \\: f(\\theta) \\text{ (objective)}                   \\\\\n   208\u2192            &\\hspace{13mm}   \\lambda \\text{ (weight decay)},\\: \\mu \\text{ (momentum)},\n   209\u2192                \\: centered, \\: \\epsilon \\text{ (epsilon)}                                       \\\\\n   210\u2192            &\\textbf{initialize} : v_0 \\leftarrow 0 \\text{ (square average)}, \\:\n   211\u2192                \\textbf{b}_0 \\leftarrow 0 \\text{ (buffer)}, \\: g^{ave}_0 Hinton.\n   237\u2192    and centered version `Generating Sequences\n   238\u2192    With Recurrent Neural Networks <https://arxiv.org/pdf/1308.0850v5.pdf>`_.\n   239\u2192    The implementation here takes the square root of the gradient average before\n   240\u2192    adding epsilon (note that TensorFlow interchanges these two operations). The effective\n   241\u2192    learning rate is thus :math:`\\gamma/(\\sqrt{v} + \\epsilon)` where :math:`\\gamma`\n   242\u2192    is the scheduled learning rate and :math:`v` is the weighted moving {
  "content": "# Plan: Extract Shared Foreach Optimizer Step Logic\n\n## Context\nPyTorch optimizers (SGD, Adam, Adagrad, etc.) all have `_multi_tensor_*` foreach implementations that handle batched parameter updates for performance. These 11+ optimizer files currently duplicate substantial amounts of common infrastructure code, making maintenance difficult and preventing consistent improvements.\n\nThe goal is to extract repeated patterns into a shared `torch/optim/_foreach.py` module while maintaining 100% backward compatibility with public APIs.\n\n## Problem Statement\n**Current state:** 11 optimizer files each contain a `_multi_tensor_*` function with 200-400+ lines of code\n- Step counter updates (CPU optimization) - duplicated 8+ times\n- Weight decay + maximize pattern - duplicated 7+ times\n- Complex number conversion - duplicated 7+ times\n- Device/dtype grouping + casting - duplicated in every file\n- Sparse gradient checks - several files\n\nThis duplication makes it difficult to:\n- Fix bugs consistently across all optimizers\n- Add features (e.g., AMP support) to all optimizers uniformly\n- Understand the core algorithm vs infrastructure code\n\n## Solution Overview\nCreate a new `torch/optim/_foreach.py` module with reusable helper functions extracted from the common patterns identified across all `_multi_tensor_*` implementations.\n\n### Key Design Principles\n1. **Don't over-engineer**: Only extract code that is actually duplicated across 2+ optimizers\n2. **Keep algorithm-specific logic in optimizer files**: Each optimizer's core algorithm stays in its file\n3. **Focus on infrastructure**: Extract device/dtype grouping, step updates, complex handling, maximize, weight decay utilities\n4. **Backward compatibility**: All public APIs remain unchanged; this is purely internal refactoring\n5. **Minimal dependencies**: New module should depend only on torch and optimizer.py utilities\n\n## Implementation Plan\n\n### Phase 1: Create `torch/optim/_foreach.py` Module\nCreate new file with shared helper functions based on duplicated patterns:\n\n**File: `/workspace/torch/optim/_foreach.py`**\n\nFunctions to extract (in priority order of duplication):\n\n1. **`_apply_weight_decay_and_maximize(grads, params, weight_decay, maximize)`**\n   - Combines the maximize negation + weight decay application pattern\n   - Handles memory reuse when both operations are needed\n   - Used in: SGD, Adam, Adagrad, Adamax, Adadelta, ASGD, RMSprop (7+ files)\n\n2. **`_update_step_counters(state_steps, is_compiling)`**\n   - Applies the CPU-specific step update optimization\n   - Avoids repeated torch.tensor() allocations\n   - Used in: Adam, Adamax, Adadelta, ASGD, RMSprop, Rprop, NAdam, RAdam (8+ files)\n\n3. **`_apply_complex_view_if_needed(has_complex, params, grads, *state_tensors)`**\n   - Converts complex tensors to real view for processing\n   - Used in: Adam, Adagrad, Adamax, Adadelta, ASGD, RMSprop, Rprop, NAdam (7+ files)\n\n4. **`_handle_capturable_bias_correction(betas, state_steps, lr, capturable, is_compiling)`**\n   - Unified capturable vs non-capturable bias correction logic\n   - Returns appropriate tensor or list of scalars\n   - Used in: Adam, Adamax, Adadelta, ASGD, RMSprop, Rprop, NAdam\n\n5. **`_validate_foreach_inputs(params, grad_scale, found_inf, differentiable, function_name)`**\n   - Centralize validation logic for foreach operations\n   - Check empty params, AMP assertions, etc.\n\n### Phase 2: Update Optimizer Files (Priority Order)\nUpdate the following files to import and use helpers from `_foreach.py`:\n\n1. **`torch/optim/sgd.py`** (_multi_tensor_sgd)\n   - Replace weight_decay + maximize logic with shared function\n   - Straightforward refactoring - minimal algorithm complexity\n\n2. **`torch/optim/adam.py`** (_multi_tensor_adam)\n   - Replace weight_decay + maximize logic\n   - Replace step update logic\n   - Replace complex number handling\n   - Keep bias correction logic (may share later)\n\n3. **`torch/optim/adamax.py`** (_multi_tensor_adamax)\n   - Same pattern as Adam\n\n4. **`torch/optim/rmsprop.py`** (_multi_tensor_rmsprop)\n   - Replace step update logic\n   - Replace complex number handling\n   - Replace weight_decay + maximize logic\n\n5. **`torch/optim/adadelta.py`** (_multi_tensor_adadelta)\n   - Similar to RMSprop pattern\n\n6. **`torch/optim/adagrad.py`** (_multi_tensor_adagrad)\n   - Has sparse handling - needs careful refactoring\n\n7. Others as time permits (ASGD, NAdam, RAdam, Rprop, Radadelta if needed)\n\n### Phase 3: Testing Strategy\n1. **Compile test** - Ensure no import/syntax errors\n2. **Run existing optimizer tests** - All should pass unchanged\n   - `python -m pytest test/test_optim.py -v` (or equivalent)\n3. **Numerical equivalence** - Foreach results vs single-tensor should match\n4. **Edge cases** - Empty params, single param, multi-device, etc.\n\n## Critical Implementation Details\n\n### Signature Patterns (Do NOT break)\nAll functions must maintain existing signatures - no changes to public optimizer APIs:\n- `sgd(params, d_p_list, momentum_buffer_list, ..., foreach=None, ...)`\n- `adam(params, grads, exp_avgs, ..., foreach=None, ...)`\n- All dispatch logic stays in optimizer files\n\n### What Stays in Optimizer Files\n- Dispatcher functions (sgd, adam, etc.) that choose single_tensor vs multi_tensor vs fused\n- Optimizer class definitions and state management\n- Algorithm-specific logic that's unique to each optimizer\n- Public docstrings and examples\n\n### What Moves to `_foreach.py`\n- Utility functions for common operations\n- Grouping/casting infrastructure\n- Step counter updates\n- Maximize + weight decay utilities\n- Complex number handling helpers\n- Validation helpers\n\n## Files to Modify\n1. **Create:** `/workspace/torch/optim/_foreach.py` (NEW)\n2. **Update:** `/workspace/torch/optim/sgd.py`\n3. **Update:** `/workspace/torch/optim/adam.py`\n4. **Update:** `/workspace/torch/optim/adamax.py`\n5. **Update:** `/workspace/torch/optim/rmsprop.py`\n6. **Update:** `/workspace/torch/optim/adadelta.py`\n7. **Update:** `/workspace/torch/optim/adagrad.py`\n8. *Others as time permits*\n\n## Success Criteria\n- [ ] `_foreach.py` module created with helper functions\n- [ ] At least 3 optimizer files (SGD, Adam, RMSprop) updated to use shared helpers\n- [ ] All existing tests pass without modification\n- [ ] Numerical equivalence verified (single-tensor vs multi-tensor outputs match)\n- [ ] Code duplication reduced by 30%+ across updated files\n- [ ] No changes to public APIs or behavior\n\n## Implementation Order\n1. Create `_foreach.py` with most duplicated helpers (weight decay + maximize)\n2. Update SGD first (simplest, good validation)\n3. Update Adam (most complex, highest impact)\n4. Update RMSprop (validates different algorithm type)\n5. Update remaining files if time permits\n\n## Validation Approach\nAfter each optimizer update:\n- Run tests for that optimizer specifically\n- Verify numerical equivalence with single-tensor implementation\n- Check import paths work correctly\n- Ensure backward compatibility\n\n## Rollback Strategy\nIf any optimizer breaks:\n- Revert that specific optimizer file to original\n- Investigate root cause in shared helper\n- Fix helper function\n- Re-attempt update\n",

no changes to public optimizer APIs:\n- `sgd(params, d_p_list, momentum_buffer_list, ..., foreach=None, ...)`\n- `adam(params, grads, exp_avgs, ..., foreach=None, ...)`\n- All dispatch logic stays in optimizer files\n\n### What Stays in Optimizer Files\n- Dispatcher functions (sgd, adam, etc.) that choose single_tensor vs multi_tensor vs fused\n- Optimizer class definitions and state management\n- Algorithm-specific logic that's unique to each optimizer\n- Public docstrings and examples\n\n### What Moves to `_foreach.py`\n- Utility functions for common operations\n- Grouping/casting infrastructure\n- Step counter updates\n- Maximize + weight decay utilities\n- Complex number handling helpers\n- Validation helpers\n\n## Files to Modify\n1. **Create:** `/workspace/torch/optim/_foreach.py` (NEW)\n2. **Update:** `/workspace/torch/optim/sgd.py`\n3. **Update:** `/workspace/torch/optim/adam.py`\n4. **Update:** `/workspace/torch/optim/adamax.py`\n5. **Update:** `/workspace/torch/optim/rmsprop.py`\n6. **Update:** `/workspace/torch/optim/adadelta.py`\n7. **Update:** `/workspace/torch/optim/adagrad.py`\n8. *Others as time permits*\n\n## Success Criteria\n- [ ] `_foreach.py` module created with helper functions\n- [ ] At least 3 optimizer files (SGD, Adam, RMSprop) updated to use shared helpers\n- [ ] All existing tests pass without modification\n- [ ] Numerical equivalence verified (single-tensor vs multi-tensor outputs match)\n- [ ] Code duplication reduced by 30%+ across updated files\n- [ ] No changes to public APIs or behavior\n\n## Implementation Order\n1. Create `_foreach.py` with most duplicated helpers (weight decay + maximize)\n2. Update SGD first (simplest, good validation)\n3. Update Adam (most complex, highest impact)\n4. Update RMSprop (validates different algorithm type)\n5. Update remaining files if time permits\n\n## Validation Approach\nAfter each optimizer update:\n- Run tests for that optimizer specifically\n- Verify numerical equivalence with single-tensor implementation\n- Check import paths work correctly\n- Ensure backward compatibility\n\n## Rollback Strategy\nIf any optimizer breaks:\n- Revert that specific optimizer file to original\n- Investigate root cause in shared helper\n- Fix helper function\n- Re-attempt update\n"

  "plan": "# Plan: Extract Shared Foreach Optimizer Step Logic\n\n## Context\nPyTorch optimizers (SGD, Adam, Adagrad, etc.) all have `_multi_tensor_*` foreach implementations that handle batched parameter updates for performance. These 11+ optimizer files currently duplicate substantial amounts of common infrastructure code, making maintenance difficult and preventing consistent improvements.\n\nThe goal is to extract repeated patterns into a shared `torch/optim/_foreach.py` module while maintaining 100% backward compatibility with public APIs.\n\n## Problem Statement\n**Current state:** 11 optimizer files each contain a `_multi_tensor_*` function with 200-400+ lines of code\n- Step counter updates (CPU optimization) - duplicated 8+ times\n- Weight decay + maximize pattern - duplicated 7+ times\n- Complex number conversion - duplicated 7+ times\n- Device/dtype grouping + casting - duplicated in every file\n- Sparse gradient checks - several files\n\nThis duplication makes it difficult to:\n- Fix bugs consistently across all optimizers\n- Add features (e.g., AMP support) to all optimizers uniformly\n- Understand the core algorithm vs infrastructure code\n\n## Solution Overview\nCreate a new `torch/optim/_foreach.py` module with reusable helper functions extracted from the common patterns identified across all `_multi_tensor_*` implementations.\n\n### Key Design Principles\n1. **Don't over-engineer**: Only extract code that is actually duplicated across 2+ optimizers\n2. **Keep algorithm-specific logic in optimizer files**: Each optimizer's core algorithm stays in its file\n3. **Focus on infrastructure**: Extract device/dtype grouping, step updates, complex handling, maximize, weight decay utilities\n4. **Backward compatibility**: All public APIs remain unchanged; this is purely internal refactoring\n5. **Minimal dependencies**: New module should depend only on torch and optimizer.py utilities\n\n## Implementation Plan\n\n### Phase 1: Create `torch/optim/_foreach.py` Module\nCreate new file with shared helper functions based on duplicated patterns:\n\n**File: `/workspace/torch/optim/_foreach.py`**\n\nFunctions to extract (in priority order of duplication):\n\n1. **`_apply_weight_decay_and_maximize(grads, params, weight_decay, maximize)`**\n   - Combines the maximize negation + weight decay application pattern\n   - Handles memory reuse when both operations are needed\n   - Used in: SGD, Adam, Adagrad, Adamax, Adadelta, ASGD, RMSprop (7+ files)\n\n2. **`_update_step_counters(state_steps, is_compiling)`**\n   - Applies the CPU-specific step update optimization\n   - Avoids repeated torch.tensor() allocations\n   - Used in: Adam, Adamax, Adadelta, ASGD, RMSprop, Rprop, NAdam, RAdam (8+ files)\n\n3. **`_apply_complex_view_if_needed(has_complex, params, grads, *state_tensors)`**\n   - Converts complex tensors to real view for processing\n   - Used in: Adam, Adagrad, Adamax, Adadelta, ASGD, RMSprop, Rprop, NAdam (7+ files)\n\n4. **`_handle_capturable_bias_correction(betas, state_steps, lr, capturable, is_compiling)`**\n   - Unified capturable vs non-capturable bias correction logic\n   - Returns appropriate tensor or list of scalars\n   - Used in: Adam, Adamax, Adadelta, ASGD, RMSprop, Rprop, NAdam\n\n5. **`_validate_foreach_inputs(params, grad_scale, found_inf, differentiable, function_name)`**\n   - Centralize validation logic for foreach operations\n   - Check empty params, AMP assertions, etc.\n\n### Phase 2: Update Optimizer Files (Priority Order)\nUpdate the following files to import and use helpers from `_foreach.py`:\n\n1. **`torch/optim/sgd.py`** (_multi_tensor_sgd)\n   - Replace weight_decay + maximize logic with shared function\n   - Straightforward refactoring - minimal algorithm complexity\n\n2. **`torch/optim/adam.py`** (_multi_tensor_adam)\n   - Replace weight_decay + maximize logic\n   - Replace step update logic\n   - Replace complex number handling\n   - Keep bias correction logic (may share later)\n\n3. **`torch/optim/adamax.py`** (_multi_tensor_adamax)\n   - Same pattern as Adam\n\n4. **`torch/optim/rmsprop.py`** (_multi_tensor_rmsprop)\n   - Replace step update logic\n   - Replace complex number handling\n   - Replace weight_decay + maximize logic\n\n5. **`torch/optim/adadelta.py`** (_multi_tensor_adadelta)\n   - Similar to RMSprop pattern\n\n6. **`torch/optim/adagrad.py`** (_multi_tensor_adagrad)\n   - Has sparse handling - needs careful refactoring\n\n7. Others as time permits (ASGD, NAdam, RAdam, Rprop, Radadelta if needed)\n\n### Phase 3: Testing Strategy\n1. **Compile test** - Ensure no import/syntax errors\n2. **Run existing optimizer tests** - All should pass unchanged\n   - `python -m pytest test/test_optim.py -v` (or equivalent)\n3. **Numerical equivalence** - Foreach results vs single-tensor should match\n4. **Edge cases** - Empty params, single param, multi-device, etc.\n\n## Critical Implementation Details\n\n### Signature Patterns (Do NOT break)\nAll functions must maintain existing signatures - no changes to public optimizer APIs:\n- `sgd(params, d_p_list, momentum_buffer_list, ..., foreach=None, ...)`\n- `adam(params, grads, exp_avgs, ..., foreach=None, ...)`\n- All dispatch logic stays in optimizer files\n\n### What Stays in Optimizer Files\n- Dispatcher functions (sgd, adam, etc.) that choose single_tensor vs multi_tensor vs fused\n- Optimizer class definitions and state management\n- Algorithm-specific logic that's unique to each optimizer\n- Public docstrings and examples\n\n### What Moves to `_foreach.py`\n- Utility functions for common operations\n- Grouping/casting infrastructure\n- Step counter updates\n- Maximize + weight decay utilities\n- Complex number handling helpers\n- Validation helpers\n\n## Files to Modify\n1. **Create:** `/workspace/torch/optim/_foreach.py` (NEW)\n2. **Update:** `/workspace/torch/optim/sgd.py`\n3. **Update:** `/workspace/torch/optim/adam.py`\n4. **Update:** `/workspace/torch/optim/adamax.py`\n5. **Update:** `/workspace/torch/optim/rmsprop.py`\n6. **Update:** `/workspace/torch/optim/adadelta.py`\n7. **Update:** `/workspace/torch/optim/adagrad.py`\n8. *Others as time permits*\n\n## Success Criteria\n- [ ] `_foreach.py` module created with helper functions\n- [ ] At least 3 optimizer files (SGD, Adam, RMSprop) updated to use shared helpers\n- [ ] All existing tests pass without modification\n- [ ] Numerical equivalence verified (single-tensor vs multi-tensor outputs match)\n- [ ] Code duplication reduced by 30%+ across updated files\n- [ ] No changes to public APIs or behavior\n\n## Implementation Order\n1. Create `_foreach.py` with most duplicated helpers (weight decay + maximize)\n2. Update SGD first (simplest, good validation)\n3. Update Adam (most complex, highest impact)\n4. Update RMSprop (validates different algorithm type)\n5. Update remaining files if time permits\n\n## Validation Approach\nAfter each optimizer update:\n- Run tests for that optimizer specifically\n- Verify numerical equivalence with single-tensor implementation\n- Check import paths work correctly\n- Ensure backward compatibility\n\n## Rollback Strategy\nIf any optimizer breaks:\n- Revert that specific optimizer file to original\n- Investigate root cause in shared helper\n- Fix helper function\n- Re-attempt update\n"

# Plan: Extract Shared Foreach Optimizer Step Logic

## Context
PyTorch optimizers (SGD, Adam, Adagrad, etc.) all have `_multi_tensor_*` foreach implementations that handle batched parameter updates for performance. These 11+ optimizer files currently duplicate substantial amounts of common infrastructure code, making maintenance difficult and preventing consistent improvements.

The goal is to extract repeated patterns into a shared `torch/optim/_foreach.py` module while maintaining 100% backward compatibility with public APIs.

## Problem Statement
**Current state:** 11 optimizer files each contain a `_multi_tensor_*` function with 200-400+ lines of code
- Step counter updates (CPU optimization) - duplicated 8+ times
- Weight decay + maximize pattern - duplicated 7+ times
- Complex number conversion - duplicated 7+ times
- Device/dtype grouping + casting - duplicated in every file
- Sparse gradient checks - several files

This duplication makes it difficult to:
- Fix bugs consistently across all optimizers
- Add features (e.g., AMP support) to all optimizers uniformly
- Understand the core algorithm vs infrastructure code

## Solution Overview
Create a new `torch/optim/_foreach.py` module with reusable helper functions extracted from the common patterns identified across all `_multi_tensor_*` implementations.

### Key Design Principles
1. **Don't over-engineer**: Only extract code that is actually duplicated across 2+ optimizers
2. **Keep algorithm-specific logic in optimizer files**: Each optimizer's core algorithm stays in its file
3. **Focus on infrastructure**: Extract device/dtype grouping, step updates, complex handling, maximize, weight decay utilities
4. **Backward compatibility**: All public APIs remain unchanged; this is purely internal refactoring
5. **Mini
... (truncated)
